---
title: "10.04 Problems: HDMI Audio Out &amp; HDMI Video Oversampling"
date: 2010-10-04
forum: Multimedia Software
---

### Post by eddieparker on 2010-10-04
Hello:

I'm a relatively new Ubuntu user - so please bear with me if I'm missing anything obvious, but I'd appreciate anyone's time in helping me with a problem I'm having.  I'm going to update this thread as I get more information, so please tune back if you're having similar problems: I'll try to update the end of this post with more details as they arise.

**[SIZE=2]The situation:[/SIZE]**

I've got a Linux box at home running Ubuntu 10.04, hooked up to my TV running Boxee.  It's recently been running using VGA and 3.5mm stereo audio, straight to my TV.  

Over the weekend we got our TV mounted, and cables ran through the wall.  To try and eliminate the number of cables, I removed the VGA and audio cables from the equation, and thought I'd go with HDMI for everything, as the quality should be better.

In the process, I've hooked up my receiver inbetween the two, and have plugged HDMI from the PC, to the receiver, and HDMI to the TV. 

Unfortunately there's some problems that have arisen in doing so:


[LIST=1]
[*]The video output appears too big for the monitor (can't see the edges)
[*]Something about the video is rather garbled at certain vertical positions
[*]HDMI audio doesn't come through or play at all.
[/LIST]

I was originally testing using Boxee itself, but to remove one variable, I've started using aplay from the command line in a gdm session to test, and still no dice.

**[SIZE=2][COLOR=Black]Current Status:[/COLOR][/SIZE]**

I've managed to hack somewhat of a solution into xorg.conf - I've configured it so as to force 1280x720, but I still get some overscan for some odd reason.  The error indicated by #2 has gone away - everything looks pixel perfect, it's just too large.  

I've "fixed" this by setting Boxee's overscan, and everything looks fine - but if/when I boot into Ubuntu normally, I can't see the edges.

Audio was 'fixed' by going with 3.5mm audio -> RCA audio splitter, but that's far from ideal.

I'd love it if people could help suggest to me avenues to explore in order to get both HDMI Audio (hopefully in 5.1!) and HDMI Video (w/o overscan issues in Ubuntu) working.  Preferably in that order. :)

**[SIZE=2]Technical Details[/SIZE]**:

I've tried to avoid my technical setup so as to give a clear picture of the issues.  If you've read this far, thanks so much!  I'll lay out the hardware in the equation, as well as software versions and configuration files - near as I can imagine are necessary.  Please don't hesitate to ask for more - I'll post them on request.

*[SIZE=2]Hardware:[/SIZE]*

TV:  Sony KDLV40XBR1 
Link: [http://esupport.sony.com/US/perl/model-home.pl?mdl=KDLV40XBR1](http://esupport.sony.com/US/perl/model-home.pl?mdl=KDLV40XBR1)
Connected to: Denon Receiver via HDMI 

Receiver: Denon 990
Link: [http://www.usa.denon.com/ProductDetails/4990.asp](http://www.usa.denon.com/ProductDetails/4990.asp)
Connected to: Boxee vs HDMI on input labelled "HDP"

PC: Custom built box
Motherboard: ZOTAC ION ITX-F-E
Link: [http://www.zotacusa.com/zotac-ionitx-f-e-atom-n330-1-6ghz-dual-core-mini-itx-intel-motherboard.html](http://www.zotacusa.com/zotac-ionitx-f-e-atom-n330-1-6ghz-dual-core-mini-itx-intel-motherboard.html)
Connected to: Denon Receiver via HDMI
Notes: This has onboard HDMI and that's what I'm using.

### Post by Grenage on 2010-10-05
The graphical issues seem to happen a fair bit, when their are receivers; I assume it's down it EDID information not being handled/received correctly.

With the audio, have you checked the simple things, like the sound applet in the menu bar?  I think mine was actually disabled after installing Ubuntu.
